<div id="review_2316809201" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2316809201" />
    <a title="alana ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12402009-alana"><img alt="alana ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599221603p2/12402009.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2316809201?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="alana ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="alana ♡" href="/user/show/12402009-alana">alana ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12402009-alana?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2316809201" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11576727233775145520">Will you hate me if I say this was legendary? Because this 100% lived up to the title.<br/>The first thing that I needed after finishing this book was a cold shower, you guys, this book is <strong>HOT. </strong>The second thing I need is either A) a time machine to transport me to next year or B) the third book immediately in my hands. Either one will do the job, just saying. I thought I had this book figured out but <strong>I SHOULD HAVE KNOWN. </strong>Dammit I should have known that things are never as they seem in the world of Ca</span>
  <span id="freeText11576727233775145520" style="display:none">Will you hate me if I say this was legendary? Because this 100% lived up to the title.<br />The first thing that I needed after finishing this book was a cold shower, you guys, this book is <strong>HOT. </strong>The second thing I need is either A) a time machine to transport me to next year or B) the third book immediately in my hands. Either one will do the job, just saying. I thought I had this book figured out but <strong>I SHOULD HAVE KNOWN. </strong>Dammit I should have known that things are never as they seem in the world of Caraval, I mean we're only warned about what? A thousand times. So I really<b> </b>should have known better.<br /><br />I was super excited for <em>Legendary</em> mainly because it is told from Tella's POV and I'm borderline in love with her. At the end of <em>Caraval</em> we find out that Tella may have gotten herself in over her head with bargains and debts she owes to not only Legend but a mysterious friend as well. I was not, however, expecting this book to literally pick up the morning after Caraval ends, so I was double the amount of thrilled upon starting this.<br /><br />Tella finds herself thrown into another game of Caraval, only this time it's real... or is it? <strong>WHO THE HECK KNOWS?!?!?!</strong> The stakes are higher than ever because if she wins she will finally find her mother and come face to face with Legend. But she also must find Legend's true identity and tell her "friend" who he is for... purposes. As usual no spoilers, so its about to get hella vague up in here. One choice betrays the other and you guys I was <strong>S W E A T I N G </strong>by the end of this book because I no idea how it was going to end or what path Tella would choose.<br /><br /><b>Here's a few of things I loved:</b><br /><br />-Who Legend really is, even though I did guess it, I am on cloud nine!<br />-At one point I was so skeptical I thought Scarlett was Legend, that's how much your mind will race while reading this<br />-We get a new setting and it was the bomb DOT COM and 10/10 on that world building<br />-The tension between Dante &amp; Tella was through the roof, hence why I needed a cold shower after this<br />-So many twists and turns and magic your head will spin<br />-We get introduced to a new character, Jacks, and I LOOOOOVED him (although don't worry I'm still Team Dante &amp; Tella forever &amp; always)<br />-Sister love is always a blast<br /><br />The one thing I had a small issue while reading this was how many times we were basically reminded what Tella's tasks were and what she would lose if she failed. It became super redundant after a while. Other than that I have zero complaints.<br /><br />All in all, it's safe to say I loved this more than <em>Caraval. </em>There's just something about Tella that I absolutely adore and I'm so happy we were able to go on this epic, magical, tantalizing journey with her. Now excuse me while I go take that cold shower and pine over the next book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11576727233775145520" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2341372689" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2341372689" />
    <a title="Larry H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h"><img alt="Larry H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577826084p2/5872506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2341372689?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry H" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h">Larry H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5872506-larry-h?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2341372689" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3154959259990338560">I'm between 4 and 4.5 stars here.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>Legendary</i>
</b>, the second book in Stephanie Garber's Caraval series, takes you on a kaleidoscopic ride full of dazzling imagery, incredible magic, and so many twists and turns, you wonder what will come with each subsequent page. It's a little dizzying, a little mesmerizing, and immensely memorable.<br/><br/>Before I get fully into the review, I must say that all I kept thinking about when reading this book was:<br/><br/><div>
<a href='https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-6HDjBB9OUts/WrsABm0bUOI/AAAAAAAAMrQ/qY4-IUnpLa8yfZnpLDs7hq8XGK5ReEb-QCLcBGAs/s1600/nph.gif' rel='nofollow noopener'><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1522205042ra/25283157.gif' width='320' height='222' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/></a><br/><br/>"Legend truly did deserve the name he'd given himself. Tella </div></span>
  <span id="freeText3154959259990338560" style="display:none">I'm between 4 and 4.5 stars here.<br><br><b>
  <i>Legendary</i>
</b>, the second book in Stephanie Garber's Caraval series, takes you on a kaleidoscopic ride full of dazzling imagery, incredible magic, and so many twists and turns, you wonder what will come with each subsequent page. It's a little dizzying, a little mesmerizing, and immensely memorable.<br><br>Before I get fully into the review, I must say that all I kept thinking about when reading this book was:<br><br><div>
<a href="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-6HDjBB9OUts/WrsABm0bUOI/AAAAAAAAMrQ/qY4-IUnpLa8yfZnpLDs7hq8XGK5ReEb-QCLcBGAs/s1600/nph.gif" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1522205042ra/25283157.gif" width="320" height="222" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br>"Legend truly did deserve the name he'd given himself. Tella wondered if Legend's games ever ended, or if his world was an endless maze of fantasy and reality that left those caught inside it forever suspended somewhere between the two."<br><br>Caraval is a magical performance which usually occurs once a year. It is a grand spectacle, where no one is sure what is real and what is merely part of the game, and yet lives are forever changed by what happens within it. Everything that happens in Caraval is orchestrated by the world-renowned Caraval Master, known only as Legend. No one knows Legend's true identity—in each game he is portrayed by someone else, taking on another form. But few have more power.<br><br>Donatella (Tella) Dragna is a feisty, almost-fearless young woman who found herself swept up in the madness of Caraval when her older sister Scarlett escaped the island on which their father was holding them both prisoner. After rescuing Scarlett from an uncertain fate and saving her from an arranged marriage sure to ruin her, the sisters made it through Caraval, and now have their lives ahead of them, finally free of their father's control. But why aren't they happy?<br><br>Tella, it seems, is determined to uncover the truth behind a painful family secret. To do so, she has made a bargain with a mysterious and dangerous criminal, who has promised to give Tella what she so desperately longs for. But of course, there is a price: this person wants to know Legend's true identity, so he can use it for nefarious purposes. There really is no perfect solution for Tella, but getting what she wants means more than almost anything, so she agrees to his bargain.<br><br>Tella must immerse herself in a special round of Caraval, where the stakes are higher than ever before. Along the way, she will tempt fate—and her own mortality; encounter a dangerous heir to the throne whose power is very real; and she'll question the intentions of everyone she comes into contact with—including her own sister. She'll also be challenged by her own heart, which she never believed would lead her to love, and even if it is, she's not sure that the person at the end of the path is worth the risks and sacrifices she must take. All the while, Tella isn't sure what is real and what is merely part of the game.<br><br>"She liked the thrill that came with taking risks. She loved the feeling of doing something bold enough to make her future hold its breath while she closed her eyes and reveled in the sensation that she'd made a choice with the power to alter the course of her life. It was the closest she ever came to holding real power."<br><br>This is a fascinating series of books, and <b><i>Legendary</i></b> is a worthy sequel to Garber's first book, <b><i>Caraval</i></b> (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1931947926?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">see my review</a>). The world she has created is fascinating, dazzling, a combination of fantasy and magic that paints pictures in your mind which are utterly glorious. I would love to see these books as movies, just to see how a filmmaker could capture this tantalizing universe.<br><br>When you're reading a book where the main character isn't sure what is real and what is artifice, things tend to get a little confusing from time to time. I had to re-read some paragraphs here and there to make sure I understood what I read. And there are a lot of different storylines and legends being unwoven in this book, so at times my attention wandered a bit until the story focused back on Tella's efforts to win Caraval. When the book hits its groove, you just want to devour it and experience it all at once.<br><br>I feel like I've been saying this a lot in my reviews recently, but this is definitely not a book for everyone. If this interests you, I'd recommend starting with <b><i>Caraval</i></b> first so you can truly appreciate the magic Garber creates here. This reminded me a little bit of Erin Morgenstern's <b><i>The Night Circus</i></b>, so if you loved that book, definitely give this series a try. I definitely hope Garber takes us back to Caraval once more!!<br><br>NetGalley and Flatiron Books provided me an advance copy of the book in exchange for an unbiased review. Thanks for making this available! <br><br>See all of my reviews at <a href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com</a>, or check out my list of the best books I read in 2017 at <a href="https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2018/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2017.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2018/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2017.html</a>.</div></span>
  <a data-text-id="3154959259990338560" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6137186894878847804">Caraval was my top book of 2017 and I was so excited to get my greedy hands on Legendary.<br/><br/>I will be 100% honest here: I wasn’t completely sold on Tella being the one who tells the story. Don’t get me wrong, I liked Tella, but I thought she was extremely flighty and I didn’t know how it would go. I need to go back and push past Stacee for even being concerned. Like Tella says in the story, everyone underestimates her and Stephanie really puts her to the test in this story. Of course there are new </span>
  <span id="freeText6137186894878847804" style="display:none">Caraval was my top book of 2017 and I was so excited to get my greedy hands on Legendary.<br /><br />I will be 100% honest here: I wasn’t completely sold on Tella being the one who tells the story. Don’t get me wrong, I liked Tella, but I thought she was extremely flighty and I didn’t know how it would go. I need to go back and push past Stacee for even being concerned. Like Tella says in the story, everyone underestimates her and Stephanie really puts her to the test in this story. Of course there are new characters and glimpses of characters in Caraval and I’m not going to say another things about them.<br /><br />Plot wise, it felt a lot more intricate to me. There are several threads in this story and it did take me a bit to settle into it, but I was captivated right from the beginning. There are swoons and kissing and magic and treachery and the ending had me hugging the book and nearly screaming.<br /><br />Overall, it was even more than I was expecting and I’ll just be over here in the corner, hoping hoping hoping that there will be more.<br /><br />**Huge thanks to Flatiron Books for providing the arc free of charge** </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18423948020420013576">3.5 stars<br/><br/>Ok, I listened to this and mostly enjoyed the story.<br/>I gotta say this, though: the descriptions of everything were so off the wall they were unintentionally hilarious. By the end of the book, I was caught between rolling my eyes and laughing out loud when Tella would say some shit like:<br/> <i>"He tasted like exquisite nightmares and stolen dreams, like the wings of fallen angels, and bottles of fresh moonlight."</i><br/>I mean, that sounds cool until you think about it for 5 seconds - what the fuck do </span>
  <span id="freeText18423948020420013576" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br><br>Ok, I listened to this and mostly enjoyed the story.<br>I gotta say this, though: the descriptions of everything were so off the wall they were unintentionally hilarious. By the end of the book, I was caught between rolling my eyes and laughing out loud when Tella would say some shit like:<br> <i>"He tasted like exquisite nightmares and stolen dreams, like the wings of fallen angels, and bottles of fresh moonlight."</i><br>I mean, that sounds cool until you think about it for 5 seconds - what the fuck do bottles of fresh moonlight taste like?!<br>Or?<br><i>“The air tasted like wonder. Like candied butterfly wings caught in sugared spiderwebs, and drunken peaches coated in luck.”</i> <br>Candied butterfly wings? Candied...? I'm genuinely torn. Is that amusing or kinda gross? And how many boozy peaches have you ever met tottering down the road?<br>WHAT ARE YOU ACTUALLY SAYING?!<br>Nothing. Your words mean nothing.<br>Hang on, let me try this out:<br><b>I'm sitting on a chair that smells like the color of metal hamburgers.</b><br>Tra-la-la!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1519052081ra/25087732.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Alright. Alright!<br>It's not like it really <i>bothered</i> me, it just made an <i>impression</i> on my reading experience that had me making faces and laughing. &lt;--which isn't a deal-breaker for me.<br>And the main story kept me interested. There's a lot of whatthefuckery happening what with the old <i>Is It/Isn't It <b>real</b>?</i> thing that was going again, only this time around Tella is the main character instead of her sister, Scarlett. And for what it <i>was</i>, it was good.<br><br><b>The book felt like the color of caramelized stuffed animals.</b> &lt;--I'm addicted and will never stop. I see now why Garber does it.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1461728140ra/18902308.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ok, so you <i>do</i> eventually find out who Legend is, but since that's the prize for winning the game, I don't think I'm giving any spoilers here. The last page leaves you wanting more even though I wasn't a fan of Tella's reaction.<br>Because <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ any idiot would have realized he loved her. DUH! He sacrificed his entire life's plan to bring your stupid ass back from that playing card. Howthefuck could you believe he had been lying about the way he felt? You couldn't. Realistically she should have been confused as to what his plan was but should have trusted that he was a good guy. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>It was angsty and stupid because PLOT REQUIREMENTS required a stupid amount of angst. And I was less than impressed.<br><br><b>Legendary's ending left me feeling like I was sitting on a trampoline made of cement the color of wallpapered beetle farts.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1494756265ra/22746597.gif" width="375" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And I'll read the next one when it comes out.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_2406614601" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2406614601" />
    <a title="• Lindsey Dahling •" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26262267-lindsey-dahling"><img alt="• Lindsey Dahling •" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578858809p2/26262267.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2406614601?book_show_action=true">Dec 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="• Lindsey Dahling •" class="user" itemprop="url" name="• Lindsey Dahling •" href="/user/show/26262267-lindsey-dahling">• Lindsey Dahling •</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2406614601" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9634429577353488657">I DID IT. I FINISHED THE DAMNED THING. And I’m going to bitch in a conflicted manner just like I did with <i>Caraval</i> AND THEN STILL ADD <i>FINALE</i> TO MY TBR LIST.<br/><br/>This book was a rollercoaster of boredom. It would build and build to potentially something interesting until the cart slowly reached the top of a hill...and then instantly raced back down through all details/explanations/anything cool in .5 seconds and go back to a flat, level track.<br/><br/>Garber did, for the most part, get rid of her annoying simil</span>
  <span id="freeText9634429577353488657" style="display:none">I DID IT. I FINISHED THE DAMNED THING. And I’m going to bitch in a conflicted manner just like I did with <i>Caraval</i> AND THEN STILL ADD <i>FINALE</i> TO MY TBR LIST.<br><br>This book was a rollercoaster of boredom. It would build and build to potentially something interesting until the cart slowly reached the top of a hill...and then instantly raced back down through all details/explanations/anything cool in .5 seconds and go back to a flat, level track.<br><br>Garber did, for the most part, get rid of her annoying similes in this one. There were only a handful of truly dear-god-just-stop-my-eyes-are-going-to-be-permanently-damaged-from-all-of-the-rolling moments. I do have to include the following examples of dumb because a) I’m concerned about Garber’s perceptions of air and b) I NEED YOU TO SUFFER WITH ME.<br><br><i>“Even the air buzzed with anticipation and excitement. Tella could feel it licking her skin, as if it wanted to drink in her frenzied emotions as well.”</i><br><br>HOW IN THE HELL IS THAT A PLEASING IMAGE? THE AIR IS BASICALLY A VAMPIRE.<br><br><i>“The air tasted like wonder. Like candied butterfly wings caught in sugared spiderwebs, and drunken peaches coated in luck.”</i><br><br>WHAT. THE. HELL. GAG. GAG. GAG.<br><br>Also, just about every object, sun stream, and/or fabric is described as “buttery” in this universe.<br><br><a href="https://beta.photobucket.com/u/whoa_its_lindsey/p/744fd3d3-b403-43bd-a727-b8892827aeff" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1544320856ra/26717264.gif" alt="61482AC2-3BB3-421E-9364-31D59DBD7570" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </a><br><br><br>The thing is, I did actually like the book. I liked it waaaaaaaay more than the first one, even though I gave them both three stars. It’s like I’m under a spell. She’s created such a fun, fantastical world with just enough mystery and intrigue that I’m willing to put up with the annoying (but much improved) writing. It’s just frustrating when an author builds and builds to this big reveal (and I’m not even necessarily talking about Legend, though multiple things about him can be included) and then the moment of truth is explained in one giant half-page exhale. This happened a lot with the character Jacks, who I think may be my favorite. I haven’t decided yet.<br><br>I will also admit that homegirl Garber did step up her game when it came to sexually charged scenes. Those were the main peaks of the boredom coaster. But, any time those parts got dangerously close to becoming interesting for the plot, she drop-kicked them right out the window into the buttery, powdered sugar tarantula air.<br><br><a href="https://beta.photobucket.com/u/whoa_its_lindsey/p/6eccf692-f63b-4135-8d81-77e3ee90dc22" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1544320856ra/26717265.gif" alt="8B6D3CAC-7A69-4DCB-9E29-E58570DEEB12" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </a><br><br>See you all in May when the last one is released. I’ll probably even WILLINGLY buy it the day of AND I STILL DON’T KNOW WHY. ✌🏻👋🏻</span>
  <a data-text-id="9634429577353488657" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2328353384" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2328353384" />
    <a title="Melissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2327397-melissa"><img alt="Melissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516632032p2/2327397.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2328353384?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa" href="/user/show/2327397-melissa">Melissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2328353384" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13481532580161183576"><em>Legendary</em> takes all the magic and the dark and the deadly and the thorned gossamer of wild invention laid over every page of <em>Caraval</em> and cranks it up to ELEVEN. Garber expands her world massively: if <em>Caraval</em> is the place where the pebble dropped in, <em>Legendary</em> is all the rings rippling outward, encompassing new terrains, new mythologies, the secret histories of characters old and new. It's darker than its predecessor. It's a little sadder. Its magic weighs heavier, and there's no more fooling our</span>
  <span id="freeText13481532580161183576" style="display:none"><em>Legendary</em> takes all the magic and the dark and the deadly and the thorned gossamer of wild invention laid over every page of <em>Caraval</em> and cranks it up to ELEVEN. Garber expands her world massively: if <em>Caraval</em> is the place where the pebble dropped in, <em>Legendary</em> is all the rings rippling outward, encompassing new terrains, new mythologies, the secret histories of characters old and new. It's darker than its predecessor. It's a little sadder. Its magic weighs heavier, and there's no more fooling ourselves: Caraval isn't just a game.<br /><br />I'm so jealous of anyone who still gets to read this book for the first time. x</span>
  <a data-text-id="13481532580161183576" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2413043763" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2413043763" />
    <a title="Hamad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54464244-hamad"><img alt="Hamad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577880699p2/54464244.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2413043763?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hamad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hamad" href="/user/show/54464244-hamad">Hamad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=2018-reads">2018-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=e-books">e-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=good-covers">good-covers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2413043763" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15206056035239818399">This review and other reviews can be found at <a href='https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2018/06/09/legendary-review/' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Book Prescription</a><br/><br/>A Buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/10148904-lily' rel='nofollow noopener'>This reading Machine</a><br/><br/><i>“If you can convince yourself it’s true, you can convince anyone.”</i><br/><br/>🌟 Caraval was a book that I didn’t enjoy very much despite having many interesting story elements, The main problem in Caraval was it being choppy and all over the place, there were many twists and events that took place in book 1. Before reading this book I had to read book 1 summary twice to get back on track. This book was m</span>
  <span id="freeText15206056035239818399" style="display:none">This review and other reviews can be found at <a href="https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2018/06/09/legendary-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Book Prescription</a><br /><br />A Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/10148904-lily" rel="nofollow noopener">This reading Machine</a><br /><br /><i>“If you can convince yourself it’s true, you can convince anyone.”</i><br /><br />🌟 Caraval was a book that I didn’t enjoy very much despite having many interesting story elements, The main problem in Caraval was it being choppy and all over the place, there were many twists and events that took place in book 1. Before reading this book I had to read book 1 summary twice to get back on track. This book was more organized, less distracting and I felt the author improved her writing style too, so what went wrong?<br /><br />🌟 let’s start with the writing style, the beginning of this book was so good and promising, that is up until a few chapters and then there is a strange shift where I felt it was written by a totally different person, then it shifts back and forth between brilliant and boring.<br /><br />🌟 The Pacing was good and despite the presence of some boring moments, I found myself wanting to know what happens, the clear ideas in this book (Honestly this was this book’s strong aspect in comparison with Caraval) helped in achieving this.<br /><br />🌟 And while book 1 focused on Scarlett, this one focuses on Tella, I don’t know how to feel about that because book 1 focuses on 1 sister while mentioning the other, while this book kind of ignores Scarlett except for a few moments here and there. And that’s not the main problem. Tella is so stupid, I mean if there was a book tag where I have to name 10 stupid characters, Tella has to be on that list! We and her by this point knows how magical and dangerous are deals and bargains during the Caraval, if you are tricked by a bargain then that’s ok, but if you know it is bad and still go into it then that’s just plain stupid!<br /><br />🌟 And speaking of Magic, where did it go? Caraval was so weird and magical and strange while this second Caraval was boring and where are all the other players? The idea I am getting is that it was specially designed for Tella which is not logical from our understanding of Caraval.<br /><br />🌟 And the plot twists were expect-able, I would have wanted more, I heard there was a surprising plot twist at the end, but I saw that whole part miles away and I even had better twists in my head!<br /><br /> <i>“…most people give up at the part of the story where things are the worst, where the situation feels hopeless. But that’s when hope is needed most.”</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="15206056035239818399" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2347827700" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2347827700" />
    <a title="Abbie (boneseasonofglass)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40819540-abbie-boneseasonofglass"><img alt="Abbie (boneseasonofglass)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506122939p2/40819540.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2347827700?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abbie (boneseasonofglass)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abbie (boneseasonofglass)" href="/user/show/40819540-abbie-boneseasonofglass">Abbie (boneseasonofglass)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40819540-abbie-boneseasonofglass?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40819540-abbie-boneseasonofglass?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40819540-abbie-boneseasonofglass?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2347827700" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11448777552871940523">Where do I start? I just want to say to begin with, that this book was amazing and it blew me away! I only finished it a few hours ago and I already want to reread it! <br/><br/>In the books, Caraval is described in a way, that as soon as it starts, you can literally feel the magic around you, and this is how I felt every time I opened up this book and started reading it. I just got lost and engulfed in the story and I felt like I could almost feel the magic coming out of the book.  <br/><br/>The plot of this book </span>
  <span id="freeText11448777552871940523" style="display:none">Where do I start? I just want to say to begin with, that this book was amazing and it blew me away! I only finished it a few hours ago and I already want to reread it! <br /><br />In the books, Caraval is described in a way, that as soon as it starts, you can literally feel the magic around you, and this is how I felt every time I opened up this book and started reading it. I just got lost and engulfed in the story and I felt like I could almost feel the magic coming out of the book.  <br /><br />The plot of this book seemed more solid than in the first book. There seemed to be a lot more at stake this time around, more mystery, and even more magic. Also the world building was wonderful, and it built more on what we learnt in the first book, with different settings in the empire being explored this time around. Also the expansion of the mythology / magic of the world was so enchanting and I just want to learn even more, which I'm sure we will in the next book hopefully! <br /><br />This book is told from the perspective of Donatella (aka 'tella'), which I preferred a lot more than Scarlet's. Tella's character seemed to have more depth and seemed more developed than Scarlet in the first book. (I'd like to add that I still really liked Scarlet). I loved seeing Tella's relationships develop with the people around her (especially Dante and Jacks), I enjoy her character so much! <br /><br />Some plot twists were kind of predictable, but at the same time, when they got revealed throughout the book, I was still shocked when they were revealed!  <br /><br />I honestly don't think there was a thing I didn't like about this book! I just wish it was longer! And I really hope there are going to be more books, because the ending was left pretty open, and there is so much that still needs resolving! There is so much more to this world that needs exploring!  </span>
  <a data-text-id="11448777552871940523" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2725062511" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2725062511" />
    <a title="Angelica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16201093-angelica"><img alt="Angelica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507050077p2/16201093.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2725062511?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angelica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angelica" href="/user/show/16201093-angelica">Angelica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=read-2019">read-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=witches-wizards-magic">witches-wizards-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=better-than-the-first">better-than-the-first</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16201093-angelica?shelf=release-2018">release-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2725062511" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8708897237869690537">Ok but like how was this book good? I don't understand! I couldn't stand Scarlett and I couldn't stand Caraval but gosh darn it, this book was so much better and I don't know why I didn't read it sooner! UGH!<br/><br/>How dare Stephanie Garber make me feel things for a series I had already given up on! I wasn't prepared to enjoy this!<br/><br/>Tella is honestly everything. I want so badly for Finale to be only about her!<br/><br/>Anyway, let's get to the review!<br/><br/>This should have been book one of this series. Where Caraval fel</span>
  <span id="freeText8708897237869690537" style="display:none">Ok but like how was this book good? I don't understand! I couldn't stand Scarlett and I couldn't stand Caraval but gosh darn it, this book was so much better and I don't know why I didn't read it sooner! UGH!<br><br>How dare Stephanie Garber make me feel things for a series I had already given up on! I wasn't prepared to enjoy this!<br><br>Tella is honestly everything. I want so badly for Finale to be only about her!<br><br>Anyway, let's get to the review!<br><br>This should have been book one of this series. Where Caraval felt like a frivolous story of magic and wishes, Legendary raises the stakes and put the very fate of the empire on the line and it was so good!<br><br><b>Where Scarlett was a whiny damsel in the first book, Tella is everything I wanted in a great character, and then some. </b>She's bold and smart and funny and just so fully herself that it was actually refreshing to read about her. Tella likes boys and pretty dresses, she likes wit and she likes winning and she doesn't apologize for it. What's more, she loves her sister with all her heart, never thinking of Scarlett as weak, even defending her sister when others would call her such. And while I might not like Scarlett, I love that she never judged Tella for being the way she was.<b> There was so much sisterly love and I was here for all of it!</b><br><br>And the boys? The tension! The banter! I was living for it. I didn't remember much of Dante from book one, other than the fact that he was an a-hole, but gosh darn it, Dante, did you shine in this book! Jacks too was an interesting character. I don't like him as a person and want to see someone (preferably Dante) put him in his place, but darn it was he entertaining! I wasn't a fan of Julian in book one so I didn't have much hope for the guys here, but <b>Stephanie Garber certainly upped her game for book two.</b><br><br>An issue I had with Caraval was the unnecessarily flowery writing. There was so much purple prose, so many overdramatic metaphors, so much randomness that it was actually distracting to me. The writing in Legendary was absolutely magical. The world was described so vividly, highlighting just how beautiful and otherworldly it all was. <b>Stephanie has certainly mastered the art of writing magic!</b><br><br>I'm honestly so impressed with this book and how much I liked it. This wasn't a five star read for me, but gosh was it good. The world building needs more work, and the magic system has absolutely explanation, and yet, I think the vagueness and mystery behind it make the story all the more mystical. A part of me hopes it never gets explained.<br><br>If you've read Caraval, I highly recommend picking this one up! I know a lot of people had mixed feelings about book one, but trust me, this book is so much better. They say Finale will be told from both Scarlett and Tella's pov, but I do hope it's mostly Tella. Never thought I'd say this, but I', highly looking forward to the last book in this series! And to think, I only read this one on a whim!<br><br>Also, here's a throwback to that time I meet Stephanie Garber! She was super sweet! I also met <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/17310926.Anna_Bright" title="Anna Bright" rel="nofollow noopener">Anna Bright</a> that day, her book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36558159.The_Beholder" title="The Beholder by Anna Bright" rel="nofollow noopener">The Beholder</a>, is coming out on June 4th!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1551054717i/27113837._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Don't I look pretty with that smile!!<br><br>Follow Me Here Too:<b> <a href="http://www.thebookcovergirls.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">My Blog</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/covergirlreads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/book-cover-girl-19339391" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin'</a> || <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookcovergirls//" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://thebookcovergirls.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/thebookcovergirls/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></b></span>

<div id="review_3364392151" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3364392151" />
    <a title="Andrea Ashwood" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51797495-andrea-ashwood"><img alt="Andrea Ashwood" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574398207p2/51797495.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3364392151?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrea Ashwood" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrea Ashwood" href="/user/show/51797495-andrea-ashwood">Andrea Ashwood</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51797495-andrea-ashwood?shelf=2020-books">2020-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3364392151" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer446999060260724408"><b>[Review Preview / Adelanto de Reseña]</b><br/><br/><b> |English|</b><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1592944171ra/29697220.gif' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Not everyone gets a true ending. There are two types of endings because most people give up at the part of the story where things are the worst, where the situation feels hopeless. But that’s when hope is needed most. Only those who persevere can find their true ending.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote>Well, everything is said...<br/><br/>I'm freaking out.<br/><br/>Did all that really just happen?<br/><br/>In other words, I've been all the damn book to find out the answers to the doubts that remain f</span>
  <span id="freeText446999060260724408" style="display:none"><b>[Review Preview / Adelanto de Reseña]</b><br><br><b> |English|</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1592944171ra/29697220.gif" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Not everyone gets a true ending. There are two types of endings because most people give up at the part of the story where things are the worst, where the situation feels hopeless. But that’s when hope is needed most. Only those who persevere can find their true ending.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote>Well, everything is said...<br><br>I'm freaking out.<br><br>Did all that really just happen?<br><br>In other words, I've been all the damn book to find out the answers to the doubts that remain from the first book and it has left me with many more. Of course a big question is resolved, but now I have like 100 more questions to add to the list.<blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>The air was full of salt and secrets.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote>At first I wasn't very convinced by the idea of ​​changing the protagonist, but I have to say that I've loved Tella, I have been able to empathize much more with her than with Scarlett, and so far I'm liking her more.<br><br>I think this book has been better than the first one, because, on the one hand there is Caraval, the game that makes its participants unable to distinguish the difference between what is real and what is not. And, on the other hand there is the new plot of The Fates and The Deck of Destiny, that I'm in love with...<br><br>If you are attracted to the plot of Caraval and you have the opportunity to read these books, I highly recommend them.<br><br>I really loved this book so much. 🥰<br><br><b>Review coming soon...</b><br><br><br><b> |Español|</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1592941809ra/29697029.gif" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>No todos obtienen un verdadero final. Hay dos tipos de finales, porque la mayoría de las personas se rinden en la parte de la historia donde las cosas empeoran, donde la situación se siente desesperada. Pero ahí es cuando más se necesita esperanza. Y solo aquellos que perseveran pueden encontrar su verdadero final.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote>Pues ya está todo dicho… <br><br>Estoy flipando.<br><br>¿De verdad acaba de ocurrir todo eso?<br><br>O sea, todo el puñetero libro para averiguar las respuestas a las dudas que quedan del primero y éste me ha dejado con el doble.<br>Por supuesto se resuelve una gran duda, también hay que decirlo, pero ahora tengo como 100 preguntas más que añadir a la lista.<blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>El aire estaba lleno de sal y secretos.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote>Al principio no me convencía mucho la idea de cambiar de protagonista, pero he de decir que Tella me ha encantado, he podido empatizar mucho más con ella que con Scarlett y hasta ahora me está gustando más.<br><br>Creo que este libro ha sido mejor que el primero, porque, por una parte está Caraval, el juego que hace perder la noción entre realidad y ficción a sus participantes y por otra parte está la nueva trama de La Baraja del Destino, la cuál encuentro fascinante.<br><br>He amado este libro.<br><br>Si os atrae la trama de Caraval y tenéis la oportunidad de leer estos libros os los recomiendo muchísimo.<br><br><b>Reseña próximamente...</b></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1ROAJEmDmyUYN3pqtNFAKyzuJ64RoY2cwE/xcUzSRAMUgsFlqjfOW+23REMqZvOGcL/2tJRuyFLaGK7c0Eo6UQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jF6NWpLCHlx/HIPmtIABb4YhDKVpabZENCDnW6N08RRNz8wbcXZLIoqcvc8qN7LC2nDdv+ym84oud7j2P+yPRg==')})
  }
